<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Exhibit&nbsp;10.21</B>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>RESTRICTED STOCK AWARD AGREEMENT</B>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Issued Pursuant to the<BR>
2004 Incentive Plan<BR>
of Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc.</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;THIS RESTRICTED STOCK AWARD AGREEMENT (&#147;Agreement&#148;), effective as of the Grant Date
(the &#147;Effective Date&#148;) set forth in the attached Restricted Stock Award Certificate (the
&#147;Certificate&#148;), represents the grant of such number of Shares of Restricted Stock set forth in the
Certificate by Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;), to the person named in the Certificate (the
&#147;Participant&#148;), subject to the terms and conditions set forth below and the provisions of the
Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc. 2004 Incentive Plan adopted by the Company&#146;s Board of Directors on March&nbsp;11,
2004 and approved by the Company&#146;s stockholders on June&nbsp;2, 2004 (the &#147;Plan&#148;).


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If there is any inconsistency between the terms of this Agreement or the Certificate (on the
one hand) and the terms of the Plan (on the other hand), the Plan&#146;s terms shall completely
supersede and replace the conflicting terms of this Agreement or the Certificate (as the case may
be). All capitalized terms shall have the meanings ascribed to them in the Plan, unless
specifically set forth otherwise herein. The parties hereto agree as follows:


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>1.&nbsp;Grant of Restricted Stock</B>. The Company hereby grants to the Participant the number of
Shares of Restricted Stock set forth in the Certificate, subject to the terms and conditions of the
Plan and this Agreement.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>2.&nbsp;Vesting Period</B>: (a) <U>In General.</U> Except as set forth in Section&nbsp;5 below, if the
Participant&#146;s employment terminates before the last vesting date set forth in the Certificate, all
Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereby that are unvested as of the date of termination of
employment shall be forfeited. Subject to the terms of this Agreement and the Plan, Shares of
Restricted Stock granted hereby shall vest as indicated in the Certificate. For the specified
vesting to occur on any vesting date set forth therein, the Participant must be continuously
employed by the Company or any of its Affiliates from the Effective Date through such vesting date.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;<U>No Partial Vesting</U>. Except as set forth in Section&nbsp;15 hereof, in no event shall
a Participant have any rights to the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder: (i)&nbsp;prior to
the date such Shares vest pursuant to the Vesting Schedule set forth in the Certificate; or (ii)
with respect to any partial Share.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>3.&nbsp;Voting Rights. </B>All Shares of Restricted Stock issued hereunder, whether vested or
unvested, shall have full voting rights accorded to outstanding Shares.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>4.&nbsp;Dividend Rights. </B>(a) <U>Cash Dividends</U>. The Participant shall be entitled to
receive any cash dividends paid with respect to Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;<U>Non-Cash Dividends</U>. Any stock dividends or other distributions or dividends of
property other than cash with respect to Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder shall be
subject to the same forfeiture restrictions and restrictions on transferability as apply to the
Restricted Stock with respect to which such property was paid.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">1
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>5.&nbsp;Nontransferability. </B>(a) <U>In General</U>. Except as may be provided in Section 5(b)
below, the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereby may not be sold, transferred, pledged,
assigned, or otherwise alienated or hypothecated, other than by will or by the laws of descent and
distribution, until such Shares have vested in accordance with Section&nbsp;2 hereof and except as
provided in the Plan. No assignment or transfer of any Shares of Restricted Stock in violation of
this Section&nbsp;5, whether voluntary or involuntary, by operation of law or otherwise, except by will
or the laws of descent and distribution or as otherwise required by applicable law, shall vest in
the assignee or transferee any interest whatsoever.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;<U>Transfers With The Consent of the Committee</U>. With the prior written consent of
the Committee, a beneficial interest in the unvested Shares of Restricted Stock awarded hereby may
be transferred by the Participant to any person or entity specified in such prior written consent
(each, a &#147;Permitted Assignee&#148;); <U>provided</U>, <U>however</U>, that if such consent is granted,
the Permitted Assignee shall be subject to the terms of this Agreement and the Plan unless an
exception is granted in writing by the Committee.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>6.&nbsp;Termination : </B>(a) <U>Death</U>. In the event a Participant dies while employed by the
Company or any of its Affiliates, all restrictions set forth herein shall lapse and any unvested
Shares of Restricted Stock held by such Participant (or his or her Permitted Assignee) shall vest
in the estate of such Participant or in any person who acquired such Shares of Restricted Stock by
bequest or inheritance, or by the Permitted Assignee.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;<U>Disability</U>. In the event a Participant ceases to perform services of any kind
(whether as an employee or Director) for the Company or any of its Affiliates due to permanent and
total disability, all restrictions set forth herein shall lapse and all unvested Shares of
Restricted Stock shall immediately vest in the Participant, or his guardian or legal
representative, or a Permitted Assignee, as of the first date of permanent and total disability (as
determined in the sole discretion of the Committee). For purposes of this Agreement, the term
&#147;permanent and total disability&#148; means the Participant is unable to engage in any substantial
gainful activity by reason of any medically determinable physical or mental impairment that can be
expected to result in death or which has lasted or can be expected to last for a continuous period
of not less than 12&nbsp;months, and the permanence and degree of which shall be supported by medical
evidence satisfactory to the Committee. Notwithstanding anything to the contrary set forth herein,
the Committee shall determine, in its sole and absolute discretion, (1)&nbsp;whether a Participant has
ceased to perform services of any kind due to a permanent and total disability and, if so, (2)&nbsp;the
first date of such permanent and total disability.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>7.&nbsp;Issuance of Restricted Stock. </B>As soon as practicable after the date of this Agreement, the
Company shall cause to be transferred on the books of the Company, Shares registered in the name of
the Company, as nominee for the Participant, evidencing the Restricted Stock covered by this
Agreement, but subject to forfeiture to the Company retroactive to the date of grant, if the
Certificate is not duly executed by the Participant and timely returned to the Company. Until the
lapse or release of all restrictions applicable to an Award of Restricted Stock, the share
certificates representing such Restricted Stock shall be held in custody by the Company or its
designee.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>8.&nbsp;Administration. </B>This Agreement and the rights of the Participant hereunder and under the
Certificate are subject to all the terms and conditions of the Plan, as the same may be amended


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">2
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">from time to time, as well as to such rules and regulations as the Committee may adopt for
administration of the Plan. It is expressly understood that the Committee is authorized to
administer, construe, and make all determinations necessary or appropriate to the administration of
the Plan, this Agreement and the Certificate, all of which shall be binding upon the Participant.
Any inconsistency between the Agreement or the Certificate (on the one hand) and the Plan (on the
other hand) shall be resolved in favor of the Plan.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>9.&nbsp;Adjustments. </B>The number of Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereby shall be subject to
adjustment in accordance with Section&nbsp;12.2 of the Plan.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>10.&nbsp;Exclusion from Pension Computations. </B>By acceptance of the Shares of Restricted Stock
granted hereunder, the Participant hereby agrees that any income or gain realized upon the receipt
or disposition of the Shares is special incentive compensation and shall not be taken into account,
to the extent permissible under applicable law, as &#147;wages&#148;, &#147;salary&#148; or &#147;compensation&#148; in
determining the amount of any payment under any pension, retirement, incentive, profit sharing,
bonus or deferred compensation plan of the Company or any of its Affiliates.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>11.&nbsp;Amendment. </B>The Committee may, with the consent of the Participant, at any time or from
time to time amend the terms and conditions of this grant of Shares of Restricted Stock. In
addition, the Committee may at any time or from time to time amend the terms and conditions of this
grant of Shares of Restricted Stock in accordance with the Plan.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>12.&nbsp;Notices. </B>Any notice which either party hereto may be required or permitted to give to the
other shall be in writing, and may be delivered personally or by mail, postage prepaid, or
overnight courier, addressed as follows: if to the Company, at its office at 1400 Old Country
Road, Westbury, New York 11590, Attn: Human Resources, or at such other address as the Company by
notice to the Participant may designate in writing from time to time; and if to the Participant, at
the address shown below his or her signature on the Certificate, or at such other address as the
Participant by notice to the Company may designate in writing from time to time. Notices shall be
effective upon receipt.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>13.&nbsp;Withholding Taxes. </B>The Company shall have the right to withhold from wages or other
amounts otherwise payable to the Participant (or a Permitted Assignee thereof), or otherwise
require the Participant or Permitted Assignee to pay, any federal, state, local or foreign income
taxes, withholding taxes, or employment taxes required to be withheld by law or regulations
(&#147;Withholding Taxes&#148;) arising as a result of the grant of any Award, the vesting of Shares of
Restricted Stock, the transfer of any Shares of Restricted Stock, the making of an election under
Section 83(b) (or any similar provision) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 (the &#147;Code&#148;), or any
other taxable event occurring pursuant to the Plan, this Agreement or the Certificate. If,
notwithstanding the foregoing, the Participant (or Permitted Assignee) shall fail to actually or
constructively make such tax payments as are required, the Company (or its Affiliates) shall, to
the extent permitted by law, have the right to deduct any such Withholding Taxes from any payment
of any kind otherwise due to such Participant or to take such other action as may be necessary to
satisfy such Withholding Taxes. In satisfaction of the requirement to pay Withholding Taxes (but
only if the Section 83(b) Election defined below has not been made with respect to the Restricted
Stock awarded hereunder), the Company, in its sole discretion, may elect to satisfy the obligation
for Withholding Taxes by retaining a sufficient number of Shares of Restricted Stock that it would
otherwise deliver on a particular vesting date equal to the amount of any Withholding Taxes due on
such vesting date.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">3
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Notwithstanding the foregoing discretion, the Company <I>shall </I>satisfy the obligation for
Withholding Taxes by retaining a sufficient number of Shares of Restricted Stock that it would
otherwise deliver on a particular vesting date equal to the amount of any Withholding Taxes due on
such vesting date, unless the Participant has either (a)&nbsp;made the Section 83(b) Election defined
below or (b)&nbsp;provided the Company with written notice at least 30&nbsp;days (or such lesser period as
may be permitted by the Company in its sole discretion) in advance of such vesting date that the
Participant will pay the Withholding Taxes in cash. For purposes of the preceding two sentences,
where the Company is to retain Shares to satisfy the obligation for Withholding Taxes, the net
amount of Shares to be delivered to the Participant on a vesting date shall equal the total number
of Shares otherwise deliverable to the Participant on such vesting date (pursuant to Section&nbsp;7
hereof and the Certificate), less such number of Shares equal to the Fair Market Value of such
Withholding Taxes (as determined in the Committee&#146;s sole discretion).



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>14.&nbsp;Registration; Legend. </B>The Company may postpone the issuance and delivery of the Shares of
Restricted Stock granted hereby until (a)&nbsp;the admission of such Shares to listing on any stock
exchange or exchanges on which Shares of the Company of the same class are then listed and (b)&nbsp;the
completion of such registration or other qualification of such Shares under any state or federal
law, rule or regulation as the Company shall determine to be necessary or advisable. The
Participant shall make such representations and furnish such information as may, in the opinion of
counsel for the Company, be appropriate to permit the Company, in light of the then existence or
non-existence with respect to such Shares of an effective Registration Statement under the
Securities Act of 1933, as amended, to issue the Shares in compliance with the provisions of that
or any comparable act.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company may cause the following or a similar legend to be set forth on each
certificate representing Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereby unless counsel for the Company
is of the opinion as to any such certificate that such legend is unnecessary:


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;THE SECURITIES REPRESENTED BY THIS CERTIFICATE MAY BE SUBJECT TO FORFEITURE AND OTHER
LIMITATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS AS SET FORTH IN A RESTRICTED STOCK AWARD AGREEMENT ON FILE WITH THE
COMPANY. IN ADDITION, THE SECURITIES REPRESENTED BY THIS CERTIFICATE MAY NOT BE OFFERED FOR SALE,
SOLD OR OTHERWISE TRANSFERRED EXCEPT PURSUANT TO AN EFFECTIVE REGISTRATION STATEMENT UNDER THE
SECURITIES ACT OF 1933, AS AMENDED (THE &#147;ACT&#148;), OR PURSUANT TO AN EXEMPTION FROM REGISTRATION UNDER
THE ACT, THE AVAILABILITY OF WHICH IS ESTABLISHED BY AN OPINION FROM COUNSEL TO THE COMPANY.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>15.&nbsp;Change in Control.</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;In the event of the occurrence of a change in control of the Company (a &#147;Change in
Control&#148;), any unvested Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder shall immediately vest. For
purposes of this Agreement, a &#147;Change in Control&#148; shall be deemed to occur if: (i)&nbsp;there shall
have occurred a change in control of the Company of a nature that would be required to be reported
in response to Item 6(e) of Schedule&nbsp;14A of Regulation&nbsp;14A promulgated under the Securities
Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, as in effect on the date hereof, whether or not the Company is
then subject to such reporting requirement, <U>provided</U>, <U>however</U>, that the foregoing
event shall not be deemed to be a Change in Control if immediately prior to such transaction the
Participant or an entity


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">4
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">of which the Participant is an executive officer, director or more than five percent equity
holder is, directly or indirectly, one of the new controlling parties; or (ii)&nbsp;the Company has
merged or consolidated with, or sold substantially all of its assets to, another company,
<U>provided</U>, <U>however</U>, that the foregoing event shall not be deemed to be a Change in
Control if immediately prior to such transaction the Participant is an executive officer, director
or more than five percent equity holder of the other party to the transaction or of any entity
directly or indirectly controlling that party to the transaction.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;Notwithstanding the foregoing, if in the event of a Change in Control, the successor
company assumes or substitutes for the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder, then the
vesting of such Restricted Stock shall not be accelerated as described in Section 15(a) hereof.
For the purposes of this Section&nbsp;15(b), the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder shall be
considered assumed or substituted for if following the Change in Control, such Shares of Restricted
Stock or any award substituted therefor (&#147;Substitute Award&#148;) confers the right to purchase or
receive, immediately prior to the Change in Control, the consideration (whether stock, cash or
other securities or property) received in the transaction constituting the Change in Control by
holders of Shares for each Share held on the effective date of such transaction (and if holders
were offered a choice of consideration, the type of consideration chosen by the holders of a
majority of the outstanding shares); <U>provided, however,</U> that if such consideration received
in the transaction constituting the Change in Control is not solely common stock of the successor
company, the Committee may, with the consent of the successor company, provide that the
consideration to be received upon the vesting of the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder
or the Substitute Award, for each Share subject thereto, will be solely common stock of the
successor company substantially equal in fair market value to the per share consideration received
by holders of Shares in the transaction constituting the Change in Control. The determination of
such substantial equality of value of consideration shall be made by the Committee in its sole
discretion and its determination shall be conclusive and binding. Notwithstanding the foregoing,
in the event of a termination of the Participant&#146;s employment in such successor company within
twenty-four (24)&nbsp;months following such Change in Control, the Shares of Restricted Stock granted
hereunder or the Substitute Award held by such Participant at the time of the Change in Control
shall vest as of the day preceding the date of termination unless the termination was made by the
successor company for cause. For purposes of this Agreement, &#147;cause&#148; shall mean either (i)
material failure by the Participant to perform his or her duties (other than as a result of
incapacity due to physical or mental illness) during his or her employment with the Company after
written notice of such breach or failure and the Participant failed to cure such breach or failure
to the Company&#146;s reasonable satisfaction within five days after receiving such written notice; or
(ii)&nbsp;any act of fraud, misappropriation, misuse, embezzlement or any other material act of
dishonesty in respect of the Company or its funds, properties, assets or other employees.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>16.&nbsp;Section&nbsp;</B><B>83(b)</B><B> Election. </B>If the Participant makes the election contemplated by Section
83(b) of the Code (a &#147;Section&nbsp;83(b) Election&#148;) (or any similar provision of federal, state or local
law) with respect to the Restricted Stock awarded hereunder, the Participant shall provide the
Company with a copy of such election within 30&nbsp;days after the date of this Agreement (or such
earlier date required by law) and otherwise comply with the provisions of this Section&nbsp;16. The
Participant hereby agrees, as a condition precedent to any issuance of Restricted Stock under this
Agreement, that on or prior to the date of filing of any Section 83(b) Election with respect to
such Restricted Stock, Participant shall satisfy the Company&#146;s Withholding Tax obligations with
respect to such Section 83(b) Election by tendering payment to the Company, in readily available
funds, of an

</DIV>

<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">amount equal to such Withholding Tax obligation (or enter into such other arrangement as shall
be acceptable to the Company to satisfy such Withholding Tax obligation).



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>17.&nbsp;No Tax Advice. </B>Participant hereby acknowledges that the Company has not provided any
specific tax advice to Participant in connection with his or her participation in the Plan.
Participant understands and acknowledges that the Section 83(b) Election is valid only if made
within 30&nbsp;days after the date of this Agreement. Participant will consult with his or her own tax
advisors with respect to any tax consequences relating to an award of Restricted Stock and
participation in the Plan.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>18.&nbsp;Miscellaneous.</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;Neither this Agreement nor the Certificate shall confer upon the Participant any right to
continuation of employment by the Company, nor shall this Agreement or the Certificate interfere in
any way with the Company&#146;s right to terminate the Participant&#146;s employment at any time.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;Except as expressly set forth herein, the Participant shall have no rights as a
stockholder of the Company with respect to the Shares of Restricted Stock subject to this Agreement
until such time as such Shares of Restricted Stock vest in accordance with Section&nbsp;2 hereof.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(c)&nbsp;This Agreement and the Certificate shall be subject to all applicable laws, rules, and
regulations, and to such approvals by any governmental agencies or national securities exchanges as
may be required.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(d)&nbsp;To the extent not preempted by federal law, this Agreement and the Certificate shall be
governed by, and construed in accordance with the laws of the State of Delaware.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(e)&nbsp;All obligations of the Company under the Plan, this Agreement and the Certificate, with
respect to the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder, shall be binding on any successor to
the Company, whether the existence of such successor is the result of a direct or indirect
purchase, merger, consolidation, or otherwise, of all or substantially all of the business and/or
assets of the Company.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(f)&nbsp;The provisions of this Agreement are severable and if any one or more provisions are
determined to be illegal or otherwise unenforceable, in whole or in part, the remaining provisions
shall nevertheless be binding and enforceable.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(g)&nbsp;By accepting this Award or other benefit under the Plan, the Participant and each person
claiming under or through the Participant shall be conclusively deemed to have indicated their
acceptance and ratification of, and consent to, any action taken under the Plan by the Company, the
Board or the Committee.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(h)&nbsp;The Participant, every person claiming under or through the Participant, and the Company
hereby waives to the fullest extent permitted by applicable law any right to a trial by jury with
respect to any litigation directly or indirectly arising out of, under, or in connection with the
Plan, this Agreement or the Certificate.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>19.&nbsp;Exculpation. </B>The Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder and all documents,
agreements, understandings and arrangements relating hereto have been issued on behalf of the
Company by officers acting on its behalf and not by any person individually. None of the officers,
Directors or stockholders of the Company nor the Directors, officers or stockholders of any
Affiliate of the Company shall have any personal liability hereunder or thereunder. The
Participant shall look solely to the assets of the Company for satisfaction of any liability of the
Company in respect of the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder and all documents,
agreements, understanding and arrangements relating hereto and will not seek recourse or commence
any action against any of the Directors, officers or stockholders of the Company or any of the
Directors, officers or stockholders of any Affiliate, or any of their personal assets, for the
performance or payment of any obligation hereunder or thereunder. The foregoing shall also apply
to any future documents, agreements, understandings, arrangements and transactions between the
parties hereto with respect to the Shares of Restricted Stock granted hereunder.

not intended to narrow, limit or affect the substance or interpretation of the provisions contained
herein.

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-3
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">






<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>MANAGEMENT&#146;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc.&#146;s (Barnes &#038; Noble or the Company) fiscal year is comprised of 52 or 53
weeks, ending on the Saturday closest to the last day of January. As used in this section, &#147;fiscal
2005&#148; represents the 52&nbsp;weeks ending January&nbsp;28, 2006, &#147;fiscal 2004&#148; represents the 52&nbsp;weeks ended
January&nbsp;29, 2005, &#147;fiscal 2003&#148; represents the 52&nbsp;weeks ended January&nbsp;31, 2004 and &#147;fiscal 2002&#148;
represents the 52&nbsp;weeks ended February&nbsp;1, 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Restatement of Financial Statements</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a result of a recent clarification from the Security and Exchange Commission, the Company
re-evaluated its lease accounting policies. Like many other companies within the retail industry
that corrected commonly accepted lease accounting practices, the Company has changed the way it
accounts for its leases, including the accounting for tenant allowances and rent holidays during
the store build-out period. As a result of its review, the Company has corrected its
lease accounting policies in fiscal 2004, and while it does not consider such corrections to be
material to any one year, has restated certain historical financial information for prior periods.
The restatement adjustments are non-cash and had no impact on revenues or total cash flows.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Consistent with common retail industry practice, the Company had previously classified tenant
allowances received as a result of store openings as a reduction in capital expenditures. The
Company has reclassified tenant allowances received from a reduction of fixed assets to an increase
in other long-term liabilities. The related amortization of such amounts has been reclassified
from a reduction of depreciation expense to a reduction of cost of sales and occupancy. Such
amortization reclassifications amounted to $32.1&nbsp;million and $28.7&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003 and 2002,
respectively.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition, consistent with industry practice, the Company had recognized the straight-line
expense for leases beginning on the earlier of the store opening date or the commencement date of
the lease, which had the effect of excluding the construction period of its stores from the
calculation of the period over which it expenses rent. In order to correct the straight-line rent
expense to include the store build-out period, in fiscal 2003 and 2002 the Company has decreased
cost of sales and occupancy and increased gross profit by $2.7&nbsp;million and $2.6&nbsp;million,
respectively, decreased operating profit and earnings before taxes and minority interest by $0.1
million and $0.8&nbsp;million, respectively, and decreased net earnings by $0.1&nbsp;million ($0.00 per
share) and $0.5&nbsp;million ($0.01 per share), respectively.The cumulative effect of such adjustments
relating to periods prior to fiscal 2002 amounting to $18.0&nbsp;million, has been recorded as a
reduction of retained earnings as of February&nbsp;2, 2002. The Company also restated the quarterly
financial information for fiscal 2003 and the first three quarters of fiscal 2004 (see Note 20 to
the Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements).


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The January&nbsp;31, 2004 balance sheet has been adjusted to reflect the combined impact of the
above restatements by increasing net property and equipment by $225.0&nbsp;million, increasing deferred
rent (other long-term liabilities) by $256.7&nbsp;million, increasing deferred tax assets by $13.2
million and decreasing retained earnings and shareholders&#146; equity by $18.6&nbsp;million.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>General</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is the nation&#146;s largest bookseller<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">1</SUP>, and as of January&nbsp;29, 2005
operates 820 bookstores. Of the 820 bookstores, 666 operate primarily under the Barnes &#038; Noble
Booksellers trade



<P>
<HR size="1" width="18%" align="left" noshade color="#000000">

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 10pt">

<TR valign="top">
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">1</SUP></TD>
    <TD width="3%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="96%">Based upon sales reported in trade
publications and public filings.</TD>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-4
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">





<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">name (32 of which were opened in fiscal 2004) and 154 operate primarily under the B. Dalton
Bookseller trade name. Barnes &#038; Noble conducts the online part of its business through
barnesandnoble.com llc (Barnes &#038; Noble.com), one of the largest sellers of books on the Internet.
Through Sterling Publishing Co., Inc. (Sterling), the Company is one of the top 25 publishers in
the nation and the industry&#146;s leading publisher of how-to books. The Company employed approximately
42,000 full- and part-time employees as of January&nbsp;29, 2005.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble is the nation&#146;s largest operator of bookstores<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">1</SUP> with 666 Barnes &#038;
Noble stores located in 49 states and the District of Columbia as of January&nbsp;29, 2005. With nearly
40&nbsp;years of bookselling experience, management has a strong sense of customers&#146; changing needs and
the Company leads book retailing with a &#147;community store&#148; concept. Barnes &#038; Noble&#146;s typical store
offers a comprehensive title base, a caf&#233;, a children&#146;s section, a music department, a magazine
section and a calendar of ongoing events, including author appearances and children&#146;s activities,
that make each Barnes &#038; Noble store an active part of its community.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble stores range in size from 10,000 to 60,000 square feet depending upon market
size, and each store features an authoritative selection of books, ranging from 60,000 to 200,000
titles. The comprehensive title selection is diverse and reflects local interests. In addition,
Barnes &#038; Noble emphasizes books published by small and independent publishers and university
presses. Bestsellers typically represent between three and five percent of Barnes &#038; Noble store
sales. Complementing this extensive on-site selection, all Barnes &#038; Noble stores provide customers
with access to the millions of books available to online shoppers while offering an option to have
the book sent to the store or shipped directly to the customer. All Barnes &#038; Noble stores are
equipped with its proprietary BookMaster in-store operating system, which enhances the Company&#146;s
merchandise-replenishment system, resulting in high in-stock positions and productivity at the
store level through efficiencies in receiving, cashiering and returns processing.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During fiscal 2004, the Company added 0.6&nbsp;million square feet to the Barnes &#038; Noble store
base, bringing the total square footage to 16.4&nbsp;million square feet, a four percent increase over
the prior year. Barnes &#038; Noble stores contributed approximately 85&nbsp;percent of the Company&#146;s total
sales in fiscal 2004. The Company plans to open between 30 and 35 Barnes &#038; Noble stores in fiscal
2005, which are expected to average 27,000 square feet in size.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At the end of fiscal 2004, the Company operated 154 B. Dalton bookstores in 43 states and the
District of Columbia. B. Dalton bookstores employ merchandising strategies that target the
mainstream consumer book market, offering a wide range of bestsellers and general-interest titles.
Most B. Dalton bookstores range in size from 2,000 to 6,000 square feet, and while they are
appropriate to the size of adjacent mall tenants, the opening of book superstores in nearby
locations continues to have a significant adverse impact on B. Dalton bookstores.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is continuing its controlled descent of its smaller format B. Dalton bookstores in
response to declining sales attributable primarily to book superstore competition. Part of the
Company&#146;s strategy has been to close underperforming stores, which has resulted in the closing of
813 B. Dalton bookstores since 1989.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On September&nbsp;15, 2003, the Company completed its acquisition of all of Bertelsmann AG&#146;s
(Bertelsmann) interest in barnesandnoble.com inc. (bn.com) and Barnes &#038; Noble.com. As a result of
the acquisition, the Company increased its economic interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com from
approximately 38&nbsp;percent to approximately 75&nbsp;percent. Subsequent to the purchase, Barnes &#038;
Noble.com employees


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-5
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">exercised 3.9&nbsp;million stock options thereby reducing the Company&#146;s economic interest in Barnes &#038;
Noble.com to approximately 73&nbsp;percent. On May&nbsp;27, 2004, the Company completed a merger (the
Merger) of bn.com with a wholly owned subsidiary of the Company. The Merger was approved by the
shareholders of bn.com at a special meeting held on May&nbsp;27, 2004. As a result of the Merger, bn.com
became a privately held company, wholly owned by the Company.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble.com sells new and used books, music and movies, and has the largest in-stock
selection of new in-print book titles of any e-commerce company. Visited by millions of users each
month, Barnes &#038; Noble.com has shipped products to more than 21&nbsp;million customers in 230 countries
since its inception in 1997. In 2004, Barnes &#038; Noble.com launched its nationwide &#147;Fast&#038;Free
Delivery&#148; service, one of the most competitive delivery offerings available from any online
retailer. Any in-stock new book, music or movie is delivered in one to three days within the
continental United States, with free delivery on purchases of $25 or more. Barnes &#038; Noble.com
provides exclusive content features such as &#147;Meet the Writers&#148;, &#147;What America&#146;s Reading&#148;, and
online reading groups, as well as third-party reviews, first chapters and table of contents, and
thousands of music clips and video trailers.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In the fourth quarter 2004 American Customer Satisfaction Index compiled by the University of
Michigan, Barnes &#038; Noble.com received the highest rating of any e-commerce company. This annual
survey is recognized as the industry&#146;s leading indicator of customer satisfaction. According to
comScore MediaMetrix December&nbsp;2004 report, Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s site was the sixteenth
most-trafficked shopping destination.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble further differentiates its product offerings from those of its competitors by
publishing books under its own imprints. The Company is one of the largest book publishers in the
world. Its subsidiary, Sterling, publishes over 1,100 new titles a year and has an active list of
over 5,000 titles. As the leading publisher of how-to books, Sterling has particular strength in
art technique, gardening, cooking, health, crafts, puzzle and game, woodworking, and house and
home. With the addition of the Sterling titles, the Company has publishing or distribution rights
to nearly 10,000 titles and offers customers high quality books at exceptional values, while
generating attractive gross margins.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2004, the Company&#146;s Board of Directors approved an overall plan for the complete
disposition of all of its Class&nbsp;B common stock in GameStop Corp. (GameStop), the Company&#146;s Video
Game operating segment. This disposition was completed in two steps. The first step was the sale of
6,107,338 shares of GameStop Class&nbsp;B common stock held by the Company to GameStop (Stock Sale) for
an aggregate consideration of $111.5&nbsp;million. The Stock Sale was completed on October&nbsp;1, 2004. The
second step in the disposition was the spin-off by the Company of its remaining 29,901,662 shares
of GameStop&#146;s Class&nbsp;B common stock (Spin-Off). The Spin-Off was completed on November&nbsp;12, 2004 with
the distribution of 0.424876232 of a share of GameStop Class&nbsp;B common stock as a tax-free
distribution on each outstanding share of the Company&#146;s common stock to the Company&#146;s stockholders
of record as of the close of business on November&nbsp;2, 2004. As a result of the Stock Sale and the
Spin-Off, GameStop is no longer a subsidiary of the Company. The disposition of all of the
Company&#146;s stockholdings in GameStop resulted in the Company presenting all historical results of
operations of GameStop as discontinued operations.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Critical Accounting Policies</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of Operations
discusses the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements, which have been prepared in accordance
with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States. The preparation of these
financial statements require management to make estimates and assumptions in certain circumstances
that affect


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-6
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">amounts reported in the accompanying consolidated financial statements and related
footnotes. In preparing these financial statements, management has made its best estimates and
judgments of certain amounts included in the financial statements, giving due consideration to
materiality. The Company does not believe there is a great likelihood that materially different amounts would be reported
related to the accounting policies described below. However, application of these accounting
policies involves the exercise of judgment and use of assumptions as to future uncertainties and,
as a result, actual results could differ from these estimates.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Other Long-Lived Assets</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s other long-lived assets include property and equipment and amortizable
intangibles. At January&nbsp;29, 2005, the Company had $804.7&nbsp;million of property and equipment, net of
accumulated depreciation, and $19.4&nbsp;million of amortizable intangible assets, net of amortization,
accounting for approximately 24.6% of the Company&#146;s total assets. The Company reviews its
long-lived assets for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the
carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable in accordance with Statement of Financial
Accounting Standards (SFAS)&nbsp;No.&nbsp;144, &#147;Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived
Assets&#148;. The Company evaluates long-lived assets for impairment at the individual store level,
which is the lowest level at which individual cash flows can be identified. When evaluating
long-lived assets for potential impairment, the Company will first compare the carrying amount of
the assets to the individual store&#146;s estimated future undiscounted cash flows. If the estimated
future cash flows are less than the carrying amount of the assets, an impairment loss calculation
is prepared. The impairment loss calculation compares the carrying amount of the assets to the
individual store&#146;s fair value based on its estimated discounted future cash flows. If required, an
impairment loss is recorded for that portion of the asset&#146;s carrying value in excess of fair value.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Goodwill and Unamortizable Intangible Assets</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At January&nbsp;29, 2005, the Company had $268.4&nbsp;million of goodwill and $78.1&nbsp;million of
unamortizable intangible assets (i.e. those with an indefinite useful life), accounting for
approximately 10.3% of the Company&#146;s total assets. SFAS No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and Other Intangible
Assets&#148;, requires that goodwill and other unamortizable intangible assets no longer be amortized,
but instead be tested for impairment at least annually or earlier if there are impairment
indicators. The Company performs a two-step process for impairment testing of goodwill as required
by SFAS No.&nbsp;142. The first step of this test, used to identify potential impairment, compares the
fair value of a reporting unit with its carrying amount. The second step (if necessary) measures
the amount of the impairment. The Company completed its annual impairment test on the goodwill in
November&nbsp;2004 and deemed that no impairment charge was necessary. The Company has noted no
subsequent indicators of impairment. The Company tests unamortizable intangible assets by comparing
the fair value and the carrying value of such assets. Changes in market conditions, among other
factors, could have a material impact on these estimates.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Closed Store Expenses</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When the Company closes or relocates a store, the Company charges unrecoverable costs to
expense. Such costs include the net book value of abandoned fixtures and leasehold improvements
and, when a store is closed, a provision for future lease obligations, net of expected sublease
recoveries. Costs associated with store closings of $6.5&nbsp;million, $5.7&nbsp;million and $9.8&nbsp;million
during fiscal 2004, 2003 and 2002, respectively, are included in selling and administrative
expenses in the accompanying consolidated statements of operations.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>52 Weeks Ended January&nbsp;29, 2005 Compared with 52 Weeks Ended January&nbsp;31, 2004</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Sales</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s sales increased $501.4&nbsp;million, or 11.5%, during fiscal 2004 to $4.874&nbsp;billion
from $4.372&nbsp;billion during fiscal 2003. The increase in sales was primarily attributable to a
$261.1&nbsp;million increase in sales at Barnes &#038; Noble stores and the increase of $268.6&nbsp;million in
sales at Barnes &#038; Noble.com. Barnes &#038; Noble store sales increased $261.1&nbsp;million, or 6.8%, during
fiscal 2004 to $4.121&nbsp;billion from $3.860&nbsp;billion during fiscal 2003 and accounted for 84.6% of
total Company sales. The 6.8% increase in Barnes &#038; Noble store sales was attributable to an
increase in comparable store sales of 3.1% coupled with the opening of 32 new stores during fiscal
2004, which contributed to a 3.7% increase in square footage. This increase was partially offset by
declining sales of B. Dalton, due to 41 store closings and a comparable store sales decline of
(2.2%) in fiscal 2004. Barnes &#038; Noble.com sales increased $268.6&nbsp;million primarily due to the full
year consolidation of Barnes &#038; Noble.com in fiscal 2004 compared with a partial year in fiscal 2003
resulting from the Company&#146;s acquisition of a controlling interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com on
September&nbsp;15, 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Cost of Sales and Occupancy</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy includes costs such as rental expense, common area
maintenance, merchant association dues and lease-required advertising partially offset by landlord
tenant


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-9
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">allowances.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of sales and occupancy increased $326.2&nbsp;million, or 10.7%, to $3.387&nbsp;billion in fiscal
2004 from $3.060&nbsp;billion in fiscal 2003, primarily due to the inclusion of Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s
cost of sales and occupancy for the full period in fiscal 2004 compared with a partial period in
fiscal 2003. As a percentage of sales, cost of sales and occupancy decreased to 69.5% in fiscal
2004 from 70.0% in fiscal 2003. This decrease was primarily attributable to the reduction in
bestseller markdowns and leverage on fixed occupancy costs.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Selling and Administrative Expenses</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling and administrative expenses increased $141.9&nbsp;million, or 15.6%, to $1,052.3&nbsp;million in
fiscal 2004 from $910.4&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003, partially due to the inclusion of Barnes &#038;
Noble.com&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy for the full period in fiscal 2004 compared with a partial
period in fiscal 2003. As a percentage of sales, selling and administrative expenses increased to
21.6% in fiscal 2004 from 20.8% in fiscal 2003. This increase was partially due to the inclusion of
Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s selling and administrative expenses for the full period in fiscal 2004
compared with a partial period in fiscal 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Depreciation and amortization increased $14.7&nbsp;million, or 8.8%, to $181.6&nbsp;million in fiscal
2004 from $166.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003. This increase was due to the inclusion of Barnes &#038;
Noble.com&#146;s depreciation and amortization for the full period in fiscal 2004 compared with a
partial period in fiscal 2003, offset by a reduction in depreciation and amortization in the Barnes
&#038; Noble stores.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Pre-Opening Expenses</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pre-opening expenses increased $0.2&nbsp;million, or 2.2%, in fiscal 2004 to $8.9&nbsp;million from $8.7
million in fiscal 2003. The slight increase in pre-opening expenses was primarily the result of
opening 32 new Barnes &#038; Noble stores during fiscal 2004, compared with 31 new Barnes &#038; Noble stores
during fiscal 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Operating Profit</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s consolidated operating profit increased $18.4&nbsp;million, or 8.2%, to $244.2
million in fiscal 2004 from $225.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003. Operating profit increased $45.6
million, or 19.6%, in fiscal 2004 excluding the operating losses of Barnes &#038; Noble.com for the full
period in fiscal 2004 compared with a partial period in fiscal 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Interest Expense, Net and Amortization of Deferred Financing Fees</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Interest expense, net of interest income, and amortization of deferred financing fees,
decreased $9.9&nbsp;million, or 47.4%, to $11.0&nbsp;million in fiscal 2004 from $20.9&nbsp;million in fiscal
2003. The decrease was primarily the result of the redemption of the Company&#146;s $300.0&nbsp;million 5.25%
convertible subordinated notes, which resulted in a reduction of the Company&#146;s average borrowings
and interest rate.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Debt Redemption Charge</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In the second quarter of fiscal 2004, the Company completed the redemption of its $300.0


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-10
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">million outstanding 5.25% convertible subordinated notes due 2009. Holders of the notes converted a
total of $17.7&nbsp;million principal amount of the notes into 545,821 shares of common stock of the
Company, plus cash in lieu of fractional shares, at a price of $32.512 per share. The Company
redeemed the balance of $282.3&nbsp;million principal amount of the notes at an aggregate redemption
price, together with accrued interest and redemption premium, of $295.0&nbsp;million. The write-off of
the unamortized portion of the deferred financing fees from the issuance of the notes and the redemption
premium resulted in a charge of $14.6&nbsp;million.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Equity in Net Loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company accounted for its approximate 38&nbsp;percent economic interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com
under the equity method through September&nbsp;15, 2003. Equity losses in Barnes &#038; Noble.com were $14.3
million in fiscal 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Income Taxes</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble&#146;s effective tax rate in fiscal 2004 increased to 43.00&nbsp;percent compared with
41.35&nbsp;percent during fiscal 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Minority Interest</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Minority interest was $1.2&nbsp;million in fiscal 2004 compared with $0.5&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003,
and relates to the approximate 26% outside interest in Calendar Club L.L.C. (Calendar Club).


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Income From Discontinued Operations</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;1, 2004, the Board of Directors of the Company approved an overall plan for the
complete disposition of all of its Class&nbsp;B common stock in GameStop, the Company&#146;s Video Game
operating segment. This disposition was completed in two steps. The first step was the sale of
6,107,338 shares of GameStop Class&nbsp;B common stock held by the Company to GameStop (Stock Sale) for
an aggregate consideration of $111.5&nbsp;million, consisting of $37.5&nbsp;million in cash and a promissory
note in the principal amount of $74.0&nbsp;million, bearing interest at a rate of 5.5% per annum,
payable when principal installments are due. The Stock Sale was completed on October&nbsp;1, 2004. The
second step in the disposition was the spin-off by the Company of its remaining 29,901,662 shares
of GameStop&#146;s Class&nbsp;B common stock (Spin-Off). The Spin-Off was completed on November&nbsp;12, 2004 with
the distribution of 0.424876232 of a share of GameStop Class&nbsp;B common stock as a tax-free
distribution on each outstanding share of the Company&#146;s common stock to the Company&#146;s stockholders
of record as of the close of business on November&nbsp;2, 2004. As a result of the Stock Sale and the
Spin-Off, GameStop is no longer a subsidiary of the Company and, accordingly, the Company will
present all historical results of operations of GameStop as discontinued operations.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-11
</DIV>

$143.4&nbsp;million (or $1.93 per share) during fiscal 2004 compared with net earnings of $151.8&nbsp;million
(or $2.07 per share) during fiscal 2003. Components of diluted earnings per share are as follows:

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>52 Weeks Ended January&nbsp;31, 2004 Compared with 52 Weeks Ended February&nbsp;1, 2003</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Sales</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s sales increased $455.6&nbsp;million, or 11.6%, during fiscal 2003 to $4.372&nbsp;billion
from $3.917&nbsp;billion during fiscal 2002. The increase in sales was primarily attributable to a
$285.4&nbsp;million increase in sales at Barnes &#038; Noble stores and the inclusion of $151.2&nbsp;million in
sales due to the consolidation of Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s results from September&nbsp;15, 2003, the date
the Company acquired a controlling interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. Barnes &#038; Noble store sales
increased $285.4&nbsp;million, or 8.0%, during 2003 to $3.860&nbsp;billion from $3.575&nbsp;billion during fiscal
2002 and accounted for 88.3% of total Company sales. The 8.0% increase in Barnes &#038; Noble store
sales was attributable to an increase in comparable store sales of 3.2% coupled with the opening of
31 new stores during fiscal 2003, which contributed to a 4.0% increase in square footage. This
increase was partially offset by declining sales of B. Dalton, due to 63 store closings and a
comparable store sales decline of (2.0%) in fiscal 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Cost of Sales and Occupancy</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy includes costs such as rental expense, common area
maintenance, merchant association dues and lease-required advertising partially offset by landlord
tenant allowances.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of sales and occupancy increased $328.9&nbsp;million, or 12.0%, to $3.060&nbsp;billion in fiscal
2003 from $2.732&nbsp;billion in fiscal 2002, partially due to the inclusion of Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s
cost of sales and occupancy since September&nbsp;15, 2003. As a percentage of sales, cost of sales and
occupancy increased to


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-12
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">70.0% in fiscal 2003 from 69.7% in fiscal 2002. This increase was primarily attributable to the inclusion of Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy since September
15, 2003.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Selling and Administrative Expenses</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling and administrative expenses increased $93.9&nbsp;million, or 11.5%, to $910.4&nbsp;million in
fiscal 2003 from $816.6&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002. As a percentage of sales, selling and
administrative expenses decreased to 20.8% in fiscal 2003 from 20.9% in fiscal 2002.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Depreciation and amortization increased $12.0&nbsp;million, or 7.7%, to $166.8&nbsp;million in fiscal
2003 from $154.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002. The increase was primarily the result of the increase in
depreciation related to the 31 new Barnes &#038; Noble stores opened during fiscal 2003 and the
inclusion of Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s depreciation since September&nbsp;15, 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Pre-Opening Expenses</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pre-opening expenses decreased $3.2&nbsp;million, or 27.4%, in fiscal 2003 to $8.7&nbsp;million from
$11.9&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002. The decrease in pre-opening expenses was primarily the result of
opening 31 new Barnes &#038; Noble stores during fiscal 2003, compared with 47 new Barnes &#038; Noble stores
during fiscal 2002.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Impairment Charge</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the first quarter of fiscal 2002, the Company deemed the decline in value in its
available-for-sale securities in Gemstar-TV Guide International, Inc. (Gemstar) and Indigo Books &#038;
Music Inc. (Indigo) to be other than temporary. The investments had been carried at fair market
value with unrealized gains and losses included in shareholders&#146; equity. The Company recorded a
non-cash impairment charge to operating earnings of $25.3&nbsp;million ($14.9&nbsp;million after taxes) to
reclassify the accumulated unrealized losses and to write down the investments to their current
fair market value at the close of business on May&nbsp;4, 2002. The investment in Gemstar was sold in
the second quarter of fiscal 2002.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Operating Profit</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s consolidated operating profit increased $49.5&nbsp;million, or 28.1%, to $225.8
million in fiscal 2003 from $176.3&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002. Operating profit increased $24.2
million, or 12.0%, in fiscal 2003 before the effect of the $25.3&nbsp;million impairment charge during
fiscal 2002.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Interest Expense, Net and Amortization of Deferred Financing Fees</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Interest expense, net of interest income, and amortization of deferred financing fees,
decreased $1.2&nbsp;million, or 5.4%, to $20.9&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003 from $22.1&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002.
The decrease was primarily the result of reduced average borrowings under the Company&#146;s senior
credit facility due to effective working capital management.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-13
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Equity in Net Loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company accounted for its approximate 38&nbsp;percent economic interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com
under the equity method through September&nbsp;15, 2003. Equity losses in Barnes &#038; Noble.com were $14.3
million and $26.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003 and 2002, respectively.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Other Expense</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2002, the Company determined that a decrease in value in certain of its equity
investments occurred which was other than temporary. As a result, other expense of $16.5&nbsp;million
during fiscal 2002 included the recognition of losses of $11.5&nbsp;million in excess of what would
otherwise have been recognized by application of the equity method in accordance with Accounting
Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;18, &#147;The Equity Method of Accounting for Investments in Common Stock&#148;.
The $16.5&nbsp;million loss in other expense was primarily comprised of $8.5&nbsp;million attributable to
iUniverse.com, $5.1&nbsp;million attributable to <I>BOOK&#174; </I>magazine and $2.4&nbsp;million attributable to enews,
inc.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Income Taxes</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble&#146;s effective tax rate in fiscal 2003 increased to 41.35&nbsp;percent compared with
40.25&nbsp;percent during fiscal 2002.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Minority Interest</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Minority interest was $0.5&nbsp;million in fiscal 2003 compared with $0.0&nbsp;million in fiscal 2002,
and relates to Calendar Club.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Income From Discontinued Operations</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;1, 2004, the Board of Directors of the Company approved an overall plan for the
complete disposition of all of its Class&nbsp;B common stock in GameStop, the Company&#146;s Video Game
operating segment as fully discussed in 52 Weeks Ended January&nbsp;29, 2005 Compared with 52 Weeks
Ended January&nbsp;31, 2004. As a result, GameStop is no longer a subsidiary of the Company and,
accordingly, the Company will present all historical results of operations of GameStop as
discontinued operations.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-14
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Seasonality</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s business, like that of many retailers, is seasonal, with the major portion of
sales and operating profit realized during the quarter which includes the holiday selling season.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Working capital requirements are generally at their highest in the Company&#146;s fiscal quarter
ending on or about January&nbsp;31 due to the higher payments to vendors for holiday season merchandise
purchases. In addition, the Company&#146;s sales and merchandise inventory levels will fluctuate from
quarter to quarter as a result of the number and timing of new store openings, as well as the
amount and timing of sales contributed by new stores.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash flows from operating activities, funds available under its revolving credit facility and
short-term vendor financing continue to provide the Company with liquidity and capital resources
for store expansion, seasonal working capital requirements and capital investments.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Cash Flow</I>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash flows provided from operating activities were $532.4&nbsp;million, $471.4&nbsp;million and $292.6
million during fiscal 2004, 2003 and 2002, respectively. In fiscal 2004, 2003 and 2002, the
increase in cash flows from operating activities was primarily attributable to improved working
capital management and an increase in net earnings.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The weighted-average age per square foot of the Company&#146;s 666 Barnes &#038; Noble stores was 7.1
years as of January&nbsp;29, 2005 and is expected to increase to approximately 8.1&nbsp;years by January&nbsp;28,
2006.


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-15
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">As the Barnes &#038; Noble stores continue to mature, and as the number of new stores opened
during the fiscal year decreases as a percentage of the existing store base, the increasing
operating profits of Barnes &#038; Noble stores are expected to generate a greater portion of the cash flows required for working
capital, including new store inventories, capital expenditures and other initiatives.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Capital Structure</I>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Strong cash flows from operations and a continued emphasis on working capital management
strengthened the Company&#146;s balance sheet in fiscal 2004.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On August&nbsp;10, 2004, the Company and certain of its wholly-owned subsidiaries entered into an
Amended and Restated Revolving Credit and Term Loan Agreement (Amended Credit Agreement) with a
syndicate of banks led by Bank of America, N.A., as administrative agent. The Amended Credit
Agreement amended the existing $500.0&nbsp;million four-year (three-year with a one-year renewal option)
senior revolving credit facility dated May&nbsp;22, 2002 (Credit Facility) to permit a new senior term
loan (Term Loan) of $245.0&nbsp;million while continuing the Credit Facility. The Credit Facility
maturity date is May&nbsp;22, 2006 and the Term Loan maturity date is August&nbsp;10, 2009. The Credit
Facility and Term Loan permit borrowings at various interest-rate options based on the prime rate
or London Interbank Offer Rate (LIBOR)&nbsp;plus an applicable margin depending upon the level of the
Company&#146;s fixed charge coverage ratio. The one-month LIBOR rate was 2.59&nbsp;percent as of the last
business day in fiscal 2004. The Company&#146;s fixed charge coverage is calculated as the ratio of
earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation, amortization and rents to interest plus rents. In
addition, the Credit Facility requires the Company to pay a commitment fee of 0.25&nbsp;percent, which
varies based upon the Company&#146;s fixed charge coverage ratio, calculated as a percentage of the
unused portion. The Company is required to pay utilization fees of 0.125&nbsp;percent and 0.25&nbsp;percent
on all outstanding loans under the Credit Facility if the aggregate outstanding loans are greater
than 33&nbsp;percent and 66&nbsp;percent, respectively, of the aggregate amount of the Credit Facility.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In accordance with the terms of the Amended Credit Agreement, as a result of the GameStop
disposition, the Credit Facility has been reduced from $500.0&nbsp;million to $400.0&nbsp;million (which may
be increased by the Company to $500.0&nbsp;million under certain circumstances). A portion of the Credit
Facility, not to exceed $100.0&nbsp;million, is available for the issuance of letters of credit.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2004, the Company redeemed its $300.0&nbsp;million outstanding 5.25&nbsp;percent convertible
subordinated notes due 2009. Holders of the notes converted a total of $17.7&nbsp;million principal
amount of the notes into 545,821 shares of common stock of the Company, plus cash in lieu of
fractional shares, at a price of $32.512 per share. The Company redeemed the balance of $282.3
million principal amount of the notes at an aggregate redemption price, together with accrued
interest and redemption premium, of $295.0&nbsp;million. The write-off of the unamortized portion of
the deferred financing fees from the issuance of the notes and the redemption premium resulted in a
charge of $14.6&nbsp;million.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Borrowings under the Company&#146;s revolving credit facility, term loan and convertible
subordinated notes averaged $276.0&nbsp;million, $342.5&nbsp;million and $377.3&nbsp;million and peaked at $392.7
million, $474.2&nbsp;million and $490.3&nbsp;million during fiscal 2004, 2003 and 2002, respectively. The
ratio of debt to equity improved to 0.21:1.00 as of January&nbsp;29, 2005 from 0.24:1.00 as of January
31, 2004.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Capital Investment</I>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital expenditures totaled $184.9&nbsp;million, $130.1&nbsp;million and $184.6&nbsp;million during fiscal
2004,


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-16
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">2003 and 2002, respectively. Capital expenditures in fiscal 2005, primarily for the opening
of between 30 and 35 new Barnes &#038; Noble stores and the opening of a new distribution center
scheduled for 2006 are expected to be approximately $190&nbsp;million, although commitment to many of
such expenditures has not yet been made.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Based on current operating levels and the store expansion planned for the next fiscal year,
management believes cash flows generated from operating activities, short-term vendor financing and
borrowing capacity under the Credit Facility will be sufficient to meet the Company&#146;s working
capital and debt service requirements, and support the development of its short- and long-term
strategies for at least the next 12&nbsp;months.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 1999, the Board of Directors authorized a common stock repurchase program for the
purchase of up to $250.0&nbsp;million of the Company&#146;s common shares. As of January&nbsp;29, 2005, the
Company has repurchased 9,007,700 shares at a cost of approximately $196.0&nbsp;million under this
program. The repurchased shares are held in treasury. Subsequent to the fiscal 2004&nbsp;year-end, the
Company completed its $250.0&nbsp;million repurchase program. On March&nbsp;24, 2005, the Company&#146;s Board of
Directors authorized a new share repurchase program of up to $200.0&nbsp;million of its common shares.
Share repurchases under this program may be made through open market and privately negotiated
transactions from time to time and in such amounts as management deems appropriate.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On September&nbsp;15, 2003, the Company completed its acquisition of all of Bertelsmann AG&#146;s
(Bertelsmann) interest in barnesandnoble.com inc. (bn.com) and barnesandnoble.com llc (Barnes &#038;
Noble.com). The purchase price paid by the Company was $165.4&nbsp;million (including acquisition
related costs) in a combination of cash and a note, equivalent to $2.80 per share in bn.com or
membership unit in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. The note issued to Bertelsmann in the amount of $82.0
million was paid in fiscal 2003. As a result of the acquisition, the Company increased its
economic interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com to approximately 75&nbsp;percent. On May&nbsp;27, 2004, the Company
completed a merger (the Merger) of bn.com with a wholly owned subsidiary of the Company. The
purchase price paid by the Company was $158.8&nbsp;million (including acquisition related costs). Under
the terms of the Merger, the holders of bn.com&#146;s outstanding common stock, other than the Company
and its subsidiaries, received $3.05 in cash for each share that they owned. The Merger was
approved by the shareholders of bn.com at a special meeting held on May&nbsp;27, 2004. As a result of
the Merger, bn.com became a privately held company, wholly owned by the Company.

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Newly Issued Accounting Pronouncements</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In May&nbsp;2004, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB)&nbsp;issued FASB Staff Position
FAS No.106-2, &#147;Accounting and Disclosure Requirements Related to the Medicare Prescription Drug,
Improvement and Modernization Act of 2003&#148; (Act), which supersedes FASB Staff Position (FSP)&nbsp;No.
106-1, to provide guidance on accounting for the effects of the Act. The Act introduces a
prescription drug benefit under Medicare Part&nbsp;D, as well as a federal subsidy to sponsors of
retiree healthcare benefit plans that provide a benefit that is at least actuarially equivalent to
Medicare Part&nbsp;D. The FSP provides guidance on measuring the accumulated postretirement benefit
obligation (APBO)&nbsp;and net periodic postretirement benefit cost, and the effects of the Act on the
APBO. In addition, the FSP addresses accounting for plan amendments and requires certain
disclosures about the Act and its effects on the financial statements. This FSP was effective for
the first interim or annual period beginning after June&nbsp;15, 2004 for public entities. The
implementation of this FSP did not have a material impact on the Company&#146;s financial statements.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In October&nbsp;2004, the FASB reached a consensus on the effective date for SFAS No.&nbsp;123R,
&#147;Share-Based Payment&#148;. While SFAS No.&nbsp;123R requires the Company to begin measuring compensation
cost for all outstanding unvested share-based awards at fair value beginning no later than the
third quarter in fiscal 2005, management currently expects to early-adopt such provisions at the
beginning of fiscal 2005. The adoption of this standard will not affect the stock-based
compensation associated with the Company&#146;s restricted stock
which is already recorded at fair
value on the date of grant and recognized over the vesting period, but will result in the
recognition of stock-based compensation in future periods for remaining unvested stock options as
of the effective date and for new stock options issued thereafter.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In November&nbsp;2004, the FASB issued SFAS No.151, &#147;Inventory Costs&#148;, which is an amendment of
Accounting Research Bulletin No.&nbsp;43, Chapter&nbsp;4, &#147;Inventory Pricing&#148;. This Statement clarifies that
abnormal amounts of idle facility expense, freight, handling costs and wasted materials (spoilage)
should be recognized as current period charges. The provisions of this statement are effective for
inventory costs incurred during the fiscal year beginning after June&nbsp;15, 2005 and are applied on a
prospective basis. The Company does not expect the impact of implementing this Statement to have a
material effect on its financial statements.
